## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt in a chemical reaction system. The rate likely depends on concentration A through standard rate law forms (power-law, rational, or composite), and may have explicit time dependence for driven or oscillatory systems.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A (first-order reaction kinetics)
- Second-order: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (second-order reaction in single species)
- nth-order: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reaction with equilibrium)
- Mixed order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme kinetics / saturation kinetics)
- Substrate inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (enzyme kinetics with substrate inhibition)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalytic reaction)
- Time-dependent forcing: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * t (rate with explicit time-dependent source)
- Exponential decay modulated: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-modulated rate constant)
- Cubic kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 + c2 * A**3 (polynomial rate law, e.g., Schlögl model)
- Fractional order: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with constant source/sink)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type cooperative kinetics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration dependence with no explicit time dependence → autonomous ODE rate law dA_dt = f(A), check if t is irrelevant
- Rate proportional to concentration raised to integer power → elementary reaction with molecularity equal to that power
- Rate that changes sign at a specific concentration → reversible reaction with equilibrium point, look for (A - A_eq) terms
- Rate with saturation at high concentration → enzyme/catalytic mechanism with denominator containing A terms
- Cubic or higher polynomial in A → multi-step reaction mechanism or bistable chemical system
- Rate that depends on both A and t explicitly → photochemical, temperature-ramped, or externally driven reaction
- Product of A with (constant - A) → autocatalytic or logistic growth kinetics where total mass is conserved
- Rate expression with A in both numerator and denominator → derived rate law from quasi-steady-state approximation of intermediates
- Negative rate at high A and positive at low A (or vice versa) → feedback mechanism or bistability in reaction network
- Square root dependence on A → rate law derived from dissociation equilibrium of a diatomic reactant (A^0.5)
